Connected-to-signed conversion.
Time from connected to signed.
Source-specific signed conversion.
Connected cohort quality.

### Vanity metrics
Connected count without signed outcome.


Cross-stage conversion principles

### Each stage conversion must preserve

Source.
Partner.
Manager.
Candidate.
Stage date.
Effective period.
Rule Pack snapshot.
Evidence.
Drop reason when known.

Conversion metrics are valid only when the denominator is clear.

### Conversion metrics become dangerous when

Stages are redefined without RuleSnapshot.
Historical rules are overwritten.
Candidate duplicates inflate counts.
Connected is treated as signed.
Interview count is treated as candidate quality.


## 10. Recruitment Risk Model

Recruitment Risk is owned by Recruitment Intelligence.

It identifies threats to future candidate flow, connected candidates, signed advisors and future advisor capacity.


Risk: Many names, few interviews

### Meaning
Relationship or source inventory is not being converted into candidate conversations.

### Possible causes
Low activation.
Poor contact execution.
Weak candidate fit.
P200 used as static list.
No trust transfer.

### Early signals
High P200 or name count with low EI.
Low contact completion.
Low appointment request.


Risk: Many interviews, few connected

### Meaning
Interview activity is not producing precontract movement.

### Possible causes
Poor candidate quality.
Weak selection.
Weak career explanation.
Poor economic clarity.
Low candidate commitment.

### Early signals
EI-to-ES drop.
EC-to-EA drop.
EA-to-connected drop.
Repeated no-shows.


Risk: Many connected, few signed

### Meaning
Recruitment handoff is not becoming advisor conversion.

### Possible causes
Precontract issue.
Expectation mismatch.
Weak commitment.
Operational friction.
Development gap.

### Recruitment position
Consumes this risk but must not own the entire downstream failure.


Risk: High dependence on FF

### Meaning
Candidate flow relies heavily on cold sources.

### Possible causes
Underused Relationship Capital.
Inactive CI.
Low PM.
Weak Market Natural activation.

### Early signals
Rising FF ratio.
Declining warm source ratio.
Low CI or RDA production.


Risk: Low PM

### Meaning
Network expansion is not happening through interview flow.

### Possible causes
Magic Question not asked.
Magic Question asked poorly.
Candidate interviews not producing trust.
No follow-up on PM names.

### Early signals
Low PM ask rate.
Low names per PM.
Low PM-to-EI conversion.


Risk: Few CI

### Meaning
The Partner lacks active influence nodes.

### Possible causes
CI relationships not identified.
CI not activated.
Poor follow-up.
Weak value exchange.

### Early signals
Low active CI count.
Long time since CI contact.
Low CI introduction rate.


Risk: Pipeline aged

### Meaning
Candidates remain too long in stage without movement.

### Possible causes
Follow-up failure.
Candidate ambiguity.
Operational delay.
Partner capacity issue.
No decision discipline.

### Early signals
Stage aging.
Repeated reschedules.
No next action.


Risk: Market Natural exhausted

### Meaning
The current reachable market is not producing new candidate movement.

### Possible causes
Overuse of same cluster.
Low network expansion.
No new CI.
No PM.
Relationship fatigue.

### Early signals
Declining warm sources.
Repeated names.
Low new cluster activation.
Low referral yield.


Risk: Activation low

### Meaning
Relationship Capital exists but is not being used.

### Possible causes
Behavior gap.
Fear of contact.
Lack of system.
No prioritization.
No coachable routine.

### Consumer
Mick should consume this as behavior signal.


Risk: Trust transfer weak

### Meaning
Sources exist but do not carry enough credibility to move candidates.

### Possible causes
Weak referrer relationship.
Poor introduction.
Low-fit referrals.
Cold-like warm labels.

### Early signals
Warm label but cold conversion.
High referral count with low EI.
Low interview acceptance.


Risk: Duplicate candidate

### Meaning
Same person appears multiple times through different sources or Partners.

### Possible causes
Capture duplication.
Weak identity resolution.
No provenance.

### Foundation dependency
CommercialPerson and provenance are required.


Risk: Manager or Partner change during process

### Meaning
Candidate ownership, attribution and coaching responsibility may become ambiguous.

### Possible causes
Assignment changes.
Office changes.
Partner changes.
Historical overwrites.

### Foundation dependency
CommercialAssignment and CommercialAttribution must preserve history.


## 11. Recruitment Forecast Review

Recruitment forecasts are suggestions.
They are not facts.

### Recruitment can forecast

Probable EI volume.
Probable ES volume.
Probable EC volume.
Probable EA volume.
Probable connected count.
Probable signed count.
Candidate flow shortage.
Stage bottleneck risk.
Source yield.
PM yield.
CI yield.
Warm source sufficiency.
Cold source dependency.
Future advisor capacity.
Recruitment inactivity risk.
Pipeline aging risk.

### Recruitment cannot forecast as fact

Guaranteed connected candidates.
Guaranteed signed advisors.
Guaranteed advisor productivity.
Guaranteed TA.
Guaranteed qualification.
Guaranteed Alta Partner.
Guaranteed compensation.
Guaranteed retention.

### Recruitment forecasts require

Historical conversion data.
Current candidate pipeline.
Source mix.
Stage aging.
Partner context.
Rule Pack snapshot.
Evidence and provenance.
Confidence label.
Clear distinction between fact and forecast.

### Forecast Confidence should decrease when

Data is incomplete.
Candidate duplicates exist.
Source attribution is unclear.
Stage dates are missing.
Rule Pack is unknown.
Historical conversion is unstable.
Pipeline is too small.
Source mix changed materially.

### Forecast guardrails

Do not present predicted signed count as confirmed.
Do not convert future signed count into compensation without compensation rules.
Do not infer productivity from recruitment alone.
Do not claim Alta Partner probability without Partner and Productivity context.
Do not hide uncertainty.

Recruitment Forecast belongs to Recruitment only when the forecast is about recruitment outcomes.

Cross-domain forecast orchestration belongs to Forecast Intelligence.


## 12. Partner Connection

Recruitment Intelligence is a foundational input for Partner Intelligence.

Partner income and promotion capacity start before compensation.
They start in the Partner's ability to open, activate and convert candidate flow into future advisors.


### Partner Intelligence consumes from Recruitment

Candidate pipeline.
Source mix.
Warm source ratio.
CI activity.
PM yield.
Interview conversion.
Connected count.
Signed outcomes.
Recruitment risk.
Future advisor capacity.
Pipeline aging.
Recruitment forecast.

### Partner Intelligence does not own

Recruitment stages.
Recruitment source quality.
Recruitment risk.
Recruitment candidate pipeline.


### Productivity Intelligence consumes from Recruitment

Signed candidate cohorts.
Connected candidate cohorts.
Source quality patterns.
Early indicators of future advisor base.

### Productivity Intelligence owns

Productivity after advisor conversion.
Activity-to-production interpretation.
Advisor productivity metrics.

### Recruitment does not own

Productivity.
TA.
Calificados.
Production.


### Forecast Intelligence consumes from Recruitment

Candidate flow.
Stage conversion.
Source yield.
Pipeline aging.
Recruitment forecast.

### Forecast Intelligence owns

Cross-domain forecasts.
Goal-to-forecast-to-gap-to-actions orchestration.

### Recruitment owns

Recruitment-domain forecast components.


### Business Planning Intelligence consumes from Recruitment

Recruitment gaps.
Future advisor capacity.
Source constraints.
Recruitment risk.
Partner pipeline sufficiency.

### Business Planning uses Recruitment to answer

Do future goals have enough candidate supply?
How many candidates are needed to support advisor growth?
Which sources must be activated?
Which recruitment gap threatens the plan?


Compensation Intelligence consumes from Recruitment only indirectly.

### Recruitment does not calculate

Commissions.
Bonuses.
Manager compensation.
Alta Partner payments.
Productivity bonuses.

Compensation may consume downstream events such as signed advisors, attribution, productivity or Rule Pack outcomes when rules require them.

Recruitment must not produce compensation values.


### Advisor Development consumes from Recruitment

Signed candidate origin.
Candidate source.
Interview path.
Commitment evidence.
Precontract handoff context.
Early development risk signals.

### Advisor Development owns

Development after candidate conversion.
Training.
Behavior progression after signing.
Skill development.


### Mick consumes from Recruitment

Recruitment activity consistency.
Activation behavior.
Follow-up behavior.
PM behavior.
CI activation behavior.
Pipeline discipline.

### Mick owns

Behavior Intelligence.

### Recruitment owns

Recruitment meaning of those behaviors.


## 13. Red Team Review

### Scenario 1
100 candidates, 0 signed.

### What breaks
If Recruitment treats candidate count as success, the model fails.

### Correct interpretation
Candidate volume is not recruitment success.
Recruitment must evaluate source quality, conversion, precontract handoff and signed outcome.

### Limit
Recruitment can identify upstream weakness or handoff weakness.
It cannot own all precontract failure.


### Scenario 2
10 signed, 0 productivity.

### What breaks
If Recruitment claims success based only on signed count, later productivity failure is hidden.

### Correct interpretation
Recruitment succeeded in candidate conversion but may have produced low-quality advisor capacity.
Productivity and Development must evaluate post-signing performance.
Recruitment should consume productivity feedback for future source quality, but not own productivity.


### Scenario 3
Many PM, bad quality.

### What breaks
If PM is treated as automatically valuable, Forge rewards noise.

### Correct interpretation
PM must be measured by yield and quality.
Names per PM is not enough.
PM-to-EI, PM-to-connected and PM-to-signed matter.


### Scenario 4
Many connected, little development.

### What breaks
Recruitment may appear successful while Development fails.

### Correct interpretation
Connected is a handoff, not final success.
Recruitment must preserve connected-to-signed and post-signing feedback, but Development owns the next phase.


### Scenario 5
Much Relationship Capital, zero activation.

### What breaks
If Relationship Capital is treated as recruitment capacity, Forge overestimates future candidate flow.

### Correct interpretation
Recruitment consumes only activated relationship access with candidate intent.
Mick should read inactivity as behavior risk.


### Scenario 6
Much P200, zero interviews.

### What breaks
If P200 is treated as recruitment artifact, Forge falsely reports recruiting strength.

### Correct interpretation
P200 is Market Natural evidence.
Recruitment begins only when P200 relationships are activated for candidate flow.


### Scenario 7
Many signed, high desertion.

### What breaks
If Recruitment ignores retention or early productivity feedback, it may keep feeding poor candidate profiles.

### Correct interpretation
Retention and development are downstream, but Recruitment should consume feedback to evaluate source and interview quality.


### Scenario 8
Cold sources produce more signed advisors than warm sources.

### What breaks
If Forge assumes warm sources always outperform cold sources, it becomes biased.

### Correct interpretation
Trust Transfer is a principle candidate, not a guarantee.
Source quality must be learned from evidence.


### Scenario 9
Candidate appears through two Partners.

### What breaks
Duplicate identity and attribution ambiguity can corrupt source metrics and Partner credit.

### Correct interpretation
CommercialPerson identity, CommercialAttribution and provenance must resolve duplicates without overwriting history.


### Scenario 10
Manager changes during recruitment.

### What breaks
If current manager is applied retroactively, historical recruitment attribution becomes false.

### Correct interpretation
Assignments must be effective-dated.
Recruitment metrics must preserve historical manager and Partner context.


### Scenario 11
Rule Pack changes interview definitions.

### What breaks
Historical conversion metrics become invalid if old stages are recalculated with new rules.

### Correct interpretation
RuleSnapshot must preserve stage definitions and evaluation rules.


### Scenario 12
Excel data is incomplete.

### What breaks
Forecasts may appear more precise than evidence supports.

### Correct interpretation
Recruitment must show confidence limits.
Missing dates, sources or stage outcomes reduce confidence.


### Red Team conclusion

The model holds if and only if Forge preserves the boundaries:

P200 is upstream evidence.
Activation is transversal capability.
Recruitment starts at candidate-intent activation.
Connected is a boundary handoff.
Signed is downstream outcome consumed by Recruitment.
Productivity and compensation remain outside Recruitment ownership.
Rule Packs define specific stage meanings.


## 14. Architecture Decision

### Recruitment Intelligence status

ARCHITECTURE LOCK

### Justification

The domain boundary is now clear.

Recruitment does not own Relationship Capital.
Recruitment does not own Market Natural.
Recruitment does not own P200.
Recruitment does not own global Relationship Activation.
Recruitment does not own Precontract.
Recruitment does not own Development.
Recruitment does not own Productivity.
Recruitment does not own Compensation.
Recruitment does not own cross-domain Forecast or Business Planning.

### Recruitment owns

RecruitmentCandidate context.
Candidate source interpretation.
Recruitment stage movement.
Recruitment funnel conversion.
Candidate Pipeline.
Recruitment Risk.
Recruitment-domain forecasts.
Recruitment-specific source quality.
Recruitment interpretation of candidate-intent activation.
Future Advisor Capacity as recruitment interpretation.

### The corrected starting point is

Relationship activated with candidate-generation intent.

### The corrected ending point is

Precontract handoff, with signed outcome consumed downstream for validation.

The remaining uncertainties are not blockers to Recruitment Architecture Lock because they belong to Rule Pack or downstream domains.

### Remaining Rule Pack dependencies

Exact SMNYL stage definitions.
Exact POP meaning.
Exact precontract criteria.
Exact connected definition.
Exact signed definition.
Exact activity thresholds.
Exact reporting formats.

These dependencies must not reopen Forge Core or Recruitment domain boundaries.


## 15. Recommended Next Step

## Recommended Next Step

Partner Intelligence

### Justification

Recruitment Intelligence now explains candidate flow.
The next architectural question is how a Partner creates, develops and scales advisor capacity from that flow.

Partner Intelligence is the most natural next domain because it consumes:

Recruitment Pipeline.
Candidate source quality.
Connected candidates.
Signed candidates.
Future Advisor Capacity.
Recruitment Risk.
Relationship Activation behavior.
Development handoff signals.

### Partner Intelligence must explain

Is the Partner opening enough future commercial capacity?
Is the Partner recruiting from strong sources?
Is the Partner converting candidates into advisors?
Is the Partner developing signed advisors into productive advisors?
Is the Partner building a sustainable unit?

### Why not Productivity Intelligence next

Productivity depends on signed advisors and development behavior.
It is downstream of Recruitment and Partner.

### Why not Forecast Intelligence next

Forecast should orchestrate multiple locked domains.
Partner context should be clarified first.

### Why not Business Planning next

Business Planning needs Partner goals, future capacity, productivity assumptions and recruitment constraints.
Partner Intelligence should define the unit-level logic first.

### Why not Advisor Development Intelligence next

Advisor Development is important, but the current thread is about Partner capacity creation.
Partner Intelligence provides the bridge between recruitment and development.


## 16. Final Verdict

Recruitment Intelligence is now architecturally hardened.

### Final status

ARCHITECTURE LOCK

### Official hardened definition

Recruitment Intelligence is the Forge domain that interprets activated relationship access with candidate-generation intent, converts it into candidate flow, measures funnel movement, evaluates source quality, detects recruitment risk and produces future advisor capacity signals for Partner, Forecast and Business Planning domains.

### Official start

When Relationship Activation occurs with candidate-generation intent.

### Official end

At Precontract handoff, with signed outcomes consumed for validation.

### Official upstream dependencies

Relationship Capital.
Market Natural.
P200 Evidence.
Relationship Activation.
Trust Transfer.
CommercialPerson.
CommercialRelationship.
CommercialAssignment.
CommercialAttribution.
EvidenceRecord.
ProvenanceRecord.
RuleSnapshot.
PeriodSnapshot.

### Official downstream consumers

Partner Intelligence.
Productivity Intelligence.
Forecast Intelligence.
Business Planning Intelligence.
Compensation Intelligence.
Advisor Development.
Mick.

### Official owner responsibilities

RecruitmentCandidate context.
Candidate Pipeline.
Source Intelligence.
Interview funnel.
Stage conversion.
Recruitment Risk.
Recruitment-domain Forecast.
Future Advisor Capacity signal.

### Official non-owner boundaries

Relationship Capital.
Market Natural.
P200.
Global Relationship Activation.
Precontract lifecycle.
Advisor contract identity.
Development.
Productivity.
Compensation.
Contest qualification.
Career progression.
Cross-domain Forecast.
Business Planning orchestration.

### Architecture conclusion

Recruitment Intelligence can now be treated as the first locked Intelligence Phase domain boundary after Foundation Lock.

Implementation remains not approved.
No code should be created from this document without a separate implementation authorization.



===== PAQ-07-PARTNER-INTELLIGENCE-DISCOVERY.md =====

# PAQ-07 Partner Intelligence Discovery

## Repository References

- [FORGE_MASTER_BUILD_TREE.md](FORGE_MASTER_BUILD_TREE.md)
- [AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md)
- [FORGE_CONSTITUTION_V3.md](FORGE_CONSTITUTION_V3.md)
- [FORGE_FOUNDATION_LOCK.md](FORGE_FOUNDATION_LOCK.md)

---


Forge OS
Principal Domain Architect Review
Partner Intelligence Discovery

### Status
ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE RECOMMENDED

### Scope
Architecture only.
No code.
No engines.
No schemas.
No UI.
No commits.


## 1. Executive Summary

Partner Intelligence is the Forge domain responsible for explaining whether a Partner is building a sustainable commercial unit.

It does not measure only recruitment.
It does not measure only productivity.
It does not measure only compensation.
It does not measure only promotion.

Partner Intelligence exists because a Partner's real job is not to personally sell more.
The Partner's real job is to create, develop, retain and scale productive commercial capacity through other people.

### The core question is

Is this Partner building a future-producing unit or only creating temporary activity?

### Recruitment Intelligence answers

Is candidate flow being created?

### Partner Intelligence must answer

Is candidate flow becoming productive, retained, scalable advisor capacity?

### The phrase from Andrey Garcia

"Un asesor es una franquicia.
La labor del Partner es abrir franquicias."

is architecturally useful, but not literally complete.

It should not be treated as a corporate definition.
It should not become a rigid constitutional principle yet.
### It should be treated as a strong operating model

A Partner builds economic units.
Each advisor can become an independent production unit.
The Partner's value is the creation and development of those units.

### The phrase is strongest when it explains

Recruitment.
Development.
Productivity creation.
Unit scaling.
Leadership pipeline.

### The phrase is weakest when it implies

Every signed advisor is already a franchise.
Every advisor has equal economic potential.
Opening many advisors is enough.
Partner success can be measured only by headcount.

### Final discovery

The true economic unit Partner Intelligence must study is not merely "advisor".

### The true economic unit is

Productive Advisor Capacity

### This includes

Signed advisor.
Activated behavior.
Development progress.
Production capability.
Retention probability.
Future leadership potential.
Economic contribution.

### Therefore

Recruitment creates future advisor supply.
Development converts signed people into productive advisors.
Productivity proves economic output.
Retention preserves the unit.
Leadership scales the unit.
Compensation reflects some outcomes, often late.

Partner Intelligence integrates those signals into one domain-level interpretation:

Is the Partner building sustainable commercial capacity?


## 2. Partner Definition

A Partner is not only a manager.

Manager is an incomplete definition because it emphasizes supervision.

A Partner is not only a coach.

Coach is incomplete because it emphasizes development but not recruitment, capacity creation or economic accountability.

A Partner is not only a recruiter.

Recruiter is incomplete because recruitment without development creates headcount without productive capacity.

A Partner is not only a builder.

Builder is useful but vague unless Forge defines what is being built.

A Partner is not only a talent developer.

Talent Developer is useful but incomplete because it starts after candidate or advisor identification.

A Partner is not only a business unit creator.

Business Unit Creator is closer because it captures economic responsibility, but it may ignore the human development dimension.

A Partner is not literally a franchise builder.

Franchise Builder is a powerful model mental, but the advisor is not always a true franchise from day one.

### Best operational definition

A Partner is a commercial capacity builder.

The Partner identifies, attracts, converts, develops, activates and retains people who can become productive advisor units.

The Partner's job is to convert human potential into durable commercial capacity.

### Compatible roles

Recruiter.
Coach.
Developer.
Capacity builder.
Commercial leader.
Pipeline owner.
Risk manager.
Talent multiplier.

### Incomplete roles

Supervisor.
Reporter.
Motivator.
Administrative manager.
Compensation recipient.

### Partner Intelligence definition

The domain that evaluates whether a Partner is building sustainable commercial capacity through recruitment, development, productivity, retention and future leadership creation.


## 3. Economic Unit Analysis

### Critical question

What economic unit is a Partner trying to create?

### Hypothesis

The advisor.

This is partially correct.

### An advisor can be

### Vendedor
Yes, but this is incomplete.
The advisor sells, but the Partner is not merely collecting salespeople.

### Productor
Yes, when the advisor generates production.
However, a signed advisor with no production is not yet a productive economic unit.

### Empleado
No as the main architecture model.
Forge should not model advisor value as employment status.

### Unidad economica
Yes, when the advisor produces, retains, renews and grows.
This is the strongest architectural model.

### Microempresa
Partially.
Useful because advisors manage relationships, pipeline, activity, clients and revenue.
Dangerous if it ignores dependency on manager, product, carrier, office, rule pack and development system.

### Franquicia
Useful as metaphor and operating model.
Not literally universal.
It helps explain duplication of a commercial model through people.
It fails if Forge assumes every signed advisor is already scalable, autonomous or economically durable.

### Otra cosa
Productive Advisor Capacity.

This is the best architectural unit.

Productive Advisor Capacity is not just a person.
It is a person plus activated behavior plus commercial capability plus development progress plus retention probability plus production output.

### Partner Intelligence must distinguish

Potential advisor.
Candidate.
Connected candidate.
Signed advisor.
Active advisor.
Productive advisor.
Retained advisor.
Leader candidate.
Manager successor.

### Destroying the advisor-as-franchise hypothesis

### Counterexample 1
A Partner signs 20 advisors and none produces.
If each advisor were a franchise, the Partner built 20 units.
Reality: the Partner created 20 weak or inactive units.

### Counterexample 2
A Partner has 3 advisors and one produces most of the unit.
The unit has production, but the Partner has concentration risk.

### Counterexample 3
A Partner has many productive advisors but no future leaders.
The unit may be productive now but not scalable.

### Counterexample 4
A Partner has high compensation because of one temporary production spike.
The unit may not be healthy.

### Counterexample 5
A Partner recruits constantly but does not retain.
The unit leaks capacity.

### Conclusion

An advisor is not automatically a franchise.
An advisor can become an economic unit.
Partner Intelligence must measure the conversion from signed person to productive advisor capacity.

### Recommended model

Candidate Flow
Signed Advisor
Active Advisor
Productive Advisor
Retained Advisor
Scalable Advisor
Leadership Candidate

The Partner's unit economics are built on the quantity, quality, productivity, durability and scalability of those advisor units.


## 4. Partner Inputs

Partner Intelligence consumes multiple upstream and downstream signals.

It does not own all of them.


Relationship Capital

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Not Partner Intelligence.
Relationship Capital is a locked transversal concept.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses Relationship Capital to understand whether the Partner has access to people, communities, influence nodes and trust paths that can support recruitment and growth.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner turning relationship access into advisor capacity?


Market Natural

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Not Partner Intelligence.
Market Natural is locked as a conceptual layer.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses Market Natural to understand available relationship surface for candidate and opportunity creation.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner activating enough of the natural market to create future capacity?


Relationship Activation

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Not Partner Intelligence.
Relationship Activation is a locked transversal capability.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses activation to understand whether relationship assets are becoming candidate flow, referral flow, introductions and commercial opportunities.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner executing the behaviors that transform access into capacity?


Recruitment Pipeline

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Recruitment Intelligence.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence consumes candidate pipeline, source mix, stage conversion, recruitment risk and recruitment forecast.

### Partner interpretation
Is there enough future advisor supply?


Connected Candidates

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Boundary between Recruitment and Precontract.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses connected candidates as evidence that recruitment is reaching precontract handoff.

### Partner interpretation
Is candidate flow becoming development workload and future advisor capacity?


Signed Advisors

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Precontract or Career lifecycle, depending on final domain ownership.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses signed advisors as evidence of capacity creation, but not proof of productive capacity.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner converting candidates into official advisor units?


Advisor Development

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Advisor Development Intelligence when defined.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence needs development progress to know whether signed advisors are becoming capable producers.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner developing people or merely signing them?


Advisor Productivity

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Productivity Intelligence.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence needs productivity to validate whether advisor units are producing economic output.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner creating productive capacity?


Retention

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Retention or Conservation-related domains depending on final domain map.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence needs retention to understand whether capacity persists.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner preserving the units being created?


Compensation

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Compensation Intelligence and Manager Compensation Intelligence.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses compensation as lagging economic evidence, not as the full definition of Partner health.

### Partner interpretation
Is economic reward aligned with sustainable capacity?


Forecasts

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Forecast Intelligence owns cross-domain forecast orchestration.
Recruitment and Productivity may own domain-level forecasts.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence consumes forecasts to understand future capacity, risk and gaps.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner likely to have enough future capacity to reach goals?


Behavior Signals

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Mick.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence needs behavior signals such as recruitment cadence, follow-up discipline, coaching rhythm, activation behavior and development consistency.

### Partner interpretation
Are the behaviors that create capacity happening consistently?


Mick Signals

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Mick owns Behavior Intelligence.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence consumes Mick signals to distinguish outcome problems from behavior problems.

### Partner interpretation
Is the Partner doing the work that creates future output?


Business Plans

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Business Planning Intelligence.

### Dependency
Partner Intelligence uses plans to evaluate whether current capacity supports declared goals.

### Partner interpretation
Can this Partner's unit realistically execute the plan?


## 5. Partner Outputs

Partner Intelligence produces domain-level interpretations of unit health, capacity and risk.


Future Advisor Capacity

Recruitment produces the raw future advisor capacity signal.
Partner Intelligence consumes and contextualizes it at unit level.

### Partner output
Whether future advisor supply is sufficient for unit growth.


Active Advisor Capacity

Partner Intelligence should produce an interpretation of how many advisors are not merely signed but actively participating in commercial work.

### Inputs
Signed advisors.
Activity signals.
Mick signals.
Development status.

### Consumer
Productivity Intelligence.
Business Planning.
Manager Intelligence.


Productive Advisor Capacity

This is the core Partner output.

### It represents
The advisor base that is generating meaningful commercial output under current rules and periods.

### Inputs
Advisor productivity.
Production events.
Activity.
Development progress.
Retention.

### Important
Productive Advisor Capacity is an interpretation.
It is not the same as production volume.


Unit Growth

Partner Intelligence produces an interpretation of whether the Partner's commercial unit is growing.

### Growth must include
New advisors.
Active advisors.
Productive advisors.
Retained advisors.
Leadership candidates.

Growth must not be measured only by headcount.


Leadership Capacity

Partner Intelligence may produce a signal about potential future leadership capacity.

This is not the same as promotion.

### It depends on
Productive advisors.
Consistency.
Development behavior.
Influence.
Potential to replicate.

This output should remain interpretation until a formal leadership domain or promotion rule exists.


Promotion Readiness

Partner Intelligence may consume promotion rules from Rule Packs to evaluate readiness.

### Ownership
Rule Pack owns promotion rules.
Partner Intelligence owns unit-level interpretation.

### Risk
Promotion readiness can be misleading if based only on current production.


Partner Risk

Partner Intelligence owns Partner Risk.

### Examples
Recruitment collapse.
Development collapse.
Productivity concentration.
Single advisor dependency.
Retention risk.
Leadership gap.
Future capacity gap.
Forecast gap.
Pipeline aging.
Source fragility.


Partner Forecast

Partner Intelligence may produce partner-domain forecast inputs.

Forecast Intelligence owns cross-domain forecast orchestration.

### Partner forecast may include
Future unit capacity.
Expected active advisors.
Expected productive advisors.
Future capacity shortage.
Development load.
Recruitment gap.
Retention risk.


Advisor Development Capacity

Partner Intelligence produces a signal about whether the Partner can develop the number and type of advisors being created.

This is not owned by Recruitment.

### It asks
Does the Partner have enough coaching bandwidth, discipline and system to convert signed advisors into productive advisors?


Recruitment Capacity

Partner Intelligence consumes Recruitment outputs but may produce Partner-level recruitment capacity interpretation.

### This asks
Can this Partner repeatedly generate enough candidate flow to sustain unit growth?


Partner Health

Partner Health is an aggregate interpretation, not a raw metric.

### It should consider
Recruitment.
Development.
Productivity.
Retention.
Concentration.
Leadership.
Behavior.
Forecast gap.

It must not be a single opaque score without explanation.


## 6. Partner Causal Chain

### The full Partner causal chain is

Relationship Capital
Market Natural
P200 Evidence
Relationship Activation
Recruitment
Candidate Flow
Connected Candidates
Signed Advisors
Advisor Development
Activity
Productivity
Retention
Leadership Emergence
Partner Unit Growth
Partner Compensation
Partner Promotion or Expansion

### Simplified chain

Access
Activation
Recruitment
Conversion
Development
Production
Retention
Scale
Economic Outcome

### Corrections to the chain

Recruitment is not the beginning of Partner success.
It is the first formal capacity-construction domain.

Signed advisors are not the end.
They are only the start of productive capacity risk.

Production is not enough.
Durable production requires retention and capacity distribution.

Compensation is not the truth.
It is a lagging economic interpretation under a Rule Pack.


Leading Indicators

Relationship activation rate.
Warm source ratio.
CI activation.
Magic Question yield.
Recruitment pipeline health.
Candidate stage conversion.
Connected candidate count.
Signed advisor trend.
Development activity.
Advisor activity consistency.
Coaching cadence.
Source diversity.
Pipeline freshness.


Lagging Indicators

Production.
Productivity.
Compensation.
Promotion.
Retained advisors.
Advisor persistence.
Leadership emergence.
Unit growth over time.


Root Causes

Insufficient relationship activation.
Weak recruitment discipline.
Poor source quality.
Low interview conversion.
Weak development system.
Poor coaching cadence.
Advisor inactivity.
Overdependence on one producer.
Weak retention.
No leadership pipeline.


False Signals

Many names.
Many candidates.
Many interviews.
Many signed advisors.
High production from one advisor.
High compensation in one period.
Large team with low activity.
Recruitment volume from low-quality sources.
Temporary promotion readiness.


## 7. Partner Success Model

Partner success is not one metric.

Partner success is sustainable capacity creation.

### A Partner is succeeding when

The Partner continuously generates candidate flow.
Candidate flow comes from quality sources.
Candidates convert into connected candidates.
Connected candidates sign.
Signed advisors activate.
Activated advisors develop.
Developed advisors produce.
Productive advisors persist.
Production is not concentrated in one person.
Future capacity exists.
Leadership potential emerges.
Compensation follows from real unit health.


### Signals that appear first

Relationship activation.
Warm source generation.
CI activity.
Magic Question yield.
Candidate flow.
Interview completion.
Connected candidates.
Development activity.
Advisor activity.


### Signals that appear later

Signed advisors.
Productivity.
Production.
Compensation.
Retention.
Leadership.
Promotion readiness.
Sustainable unit growth.


### Signals that deceive

Many candidates without conversion.
Many signed advisors without activity.
Many advisors without productivity.
High production from one advisor.
High compensation from temporary rule effects.
Large pipeline with old candidates.
High activity with no conversion.
Warm source labels with cold-source behavior.


Examples

### Many candidates
Positive only if they convert and come from sources with evidence of quality.

### Many signed
Positive only if they activate and develop.

### High production
Positive only if distributed and repeatable.

### Many advisors
Positive only if active, productive and retained.

### Many active advisors
Positive if activity is connected to production and development.

### Many qualified advisors
Positive if qualification is rule-backed, repeatable and not concentrated.

### Many leaders
Strong signal if leadership capacity is real and tied to productive behavior.

### Core success question

Can this Partner keep opening, developing and preserving productive advisor capacity?


## 8. Partner Failure Model

Partner failure usually appears late in compensation but begins earlier in behavior and capacity creation.


### Failure cause
Does not recruit.

### Root cause
No candidate flow.
Low relationship activation.
Weak source discipline.

### Symptoms
Empty pipeline.
Few interviews.
Few connected.
Future capacity gap.

### Consequences
No new advisor supply.
Unit ages.
Production depends on existing advisors.
Partner growth stalls.


### Failure cause
Does not develop.

### Root cause
Signed advisors are not converted into productive advisors.

### Symptoms
Many signed.
Low activity.
Low first production.
Low persistence.
Low confidence.

### Consequences
Recruitment effort is wasted.
Advisor attrition rises.
Partner capacity does not compound.


### Failure cause
Does not retain.

### Root cause
Advisor units are not durable.

### Symptoms
Advisor churn.
Production drops after initial periods.
Repeated replacement cycle.

### Consequences
Unit never compounds.
Recruitment must constantly refill losses.


### Failure cause
Does not activate relationships.

### Root cause
Relationship Capital exists but is not converted into candidate or opportunity flow.

### Symptoms
Large P200.
Low calls.
Low PM.
Low CI.
Low interviews.

### Consequences
Capacity remains latent.
Recruitment collapses.


### Failure cause
Does not generate trust.

### Root cause
Sources lack credibility or introductions are weak.

### Symptoms
Cold conversion behavior.
No-shows.
Low acceptance.
Low stage conversion.

### Consequences
High effort, low yield.


### Failure cause
Depends on few people.

### Root cause
Production concentration.

### Symptoms
One or two advisors dominate output.
Team metrics look strong but fragile.

### Consequences
One departure or slowdown can collapse the unit.


### Failure cause
Depends on FF.

### Root cause
Weak warm source activation.

### Symptoms
High cold source ratio.
Low trust transfer.
Low conversion.

### Consequences
Recruitment cost rises.
Predictability declines.


### Failure cause
Does not generate leaders.

### Root cause
Advisor base does not produce future capacity multipliers.

### Symptoms
Productive advisors but no leadership candidates.
Partner remains bottleneck.

### Consequences
Unit cannot scale beyond direct Partner capacity.


## 9. Partner Risk Model

Partner Risk is owned by Partner Intelligence.

It integrates risks from Recruitment, Development, Productivity, Retention, Behavior and Forecast domains.


Recruitment Collapse

### Definition
Future candidate flow is insufficient.

### Signals
Low candidate pipeline.
Low warm sources.
Few interviews.
Few connected.
Pipeline aging.

### Impact
Future advisor capacity shortage.


Development Collapse

### Definition
Signed advisors are not becoming active or productive.

### Signals
Many signed with low activity.
Poor early development completion.
Weak coaching cadence.
Low first production.

### Impact
Recruitment does not convert into economic capacity.


Productivity Concentration

### Definition
Unit production depends on too few advisors.

### Signals
High production share from one advisor.
Low median productivity.
Large gap between top producer and rest.

### Impact
Unit is fragile even if current production is high.


Single Advisor Dependency

### Definition
Partner outcome is materially dependent on one advisor.

### Signals
One advisor drives qualification, compensation or promotion readiness.

### Impact
Loss or slowdown of one advisor damages unit health.


Retention Risk

### Definition
Advisor capacity may not persist.

### Signals
Early inactivity.
Low development engagement.
Declining production.
Low relationship activation.
Low persistence indicators.

### Impact
Unit loses accumulated capacity.


Leadership Gap

### Definition
No emerging advisors can become multipliers.

### Signals
No productive advisors with influence.
No advisors developing others.
No future Partner candidates.

### Impact
Unit cannot scale beyond current Partner.


Future Capacity Gap

### Definition
Current recruitment and development are insufficient for future goals.

### Signals
Forecasted advisor supply below goal.
Connected count below needed.
Signed count below needed.
Development backlog.

### Impact
Business plan becomes unrealistic.


Forecast Gap

### Definition
Partner expected outcomes differ materially from current trajectory.

### Signals
Goal higher than capacity.
Pipeline below forecast need.
Productivity below assumption.
Retention lower than plan.

### Impact
Partner needs action before lagging metrics fail.


Pipeline Aging

### Definition
Candidates or advisors are stuck too long without movement.

### Signals
Old candidates.
Old connected candidates.
Signed advisors with no early activity.

### Impact
Future capacity decays.


Source Fragility

### Definition
Recruitment depends on weak or narrow source channels.

### Signals
High FF.
Low CI.
Low PM.
One referrer dominates.
One cluster dominates.

### Impact
Candidate supply becomes fragile.


Development Bandwidth Risk

### Definition
Partner signs more people than they can develop.

### Signals
High signed count with low coaching cadence.
Delayed follow-up.
Inconsistent development progress.

### Impact
Advisor conversion quality declines.


Compensation Mirage

### Definition
Partner compensation looks strong while underlying unit health is weak.

### Signals
High payout from concentrated or temporary production.
Low recruitment.
Low retention.
Weak future pipeline.

### Impact
Partner may appear successful while future capacity deteriorates.


## 10. Partner Forecast Review

Partner forecasts are suggestions.
They are not facts.

### Partner Intelligence can forecast

Future advisor count.
Future active advisor count.
Future productive advisor capacity.
Future unit capacity.
Future recruitment gap.
Future development gap.
Future retention risk.
Future productivity concentration risk.
Future promotion readiness.
Future leadership gap.
Future income capacity range.
Future coaching load.
Future unit fragility.

### Partner Intelligence cannot forecast as fact

Guaranteed production.
Guaranteed compensation.
Guaranteed promotion.
Guaranteed advisor retention.
Guaranteed leadership emergence.
Guaranteed Alta Partner.
Guaranteed qualification.
Guaranteed productivity.

### Forecasts require

Recruitment pipeline.
Connected candidates.
Signed advisors.
Development status.
Advisor activity.
Productivity history.
Retention history.
Behavior signals.
Rule Pack snapshot.
Period snapshot.
Evidence.
Confidence.

### Forecast confidence decreases when

Recruitment data is incomplete.
Signed advisor data is missing.
Productivity history is too short.
One advisor dominates outcomes.
Rule Pack context is unclear.
Development signals are missing.
Retention signals are weak.
Manager or Partner assignment changed.

### Partner forecast must not

Convert future capacity into guaranteed income without Compensation rules.
Treat signed advisors as productive advisors.
Treat candidate flow as future production.
Treat promotion readiness as promotion certainty.
Hide concentration risk.

### Forecast vs Fact

### Fact
Signed advisor exists.
Candidate completed stage.
Production event occurred.
Commission was paid.
Advisor is assigned to Partner for a period.

### Forecast
Advisor may become productive.
Unit may reach capacity.
Partner may qualify.
Future compensation may increase.
Future recruitment gap may occur.


## 11. Partner Vs Productivity

Partner Intelligence and Productivity Intelligence are related but not the same.


### Partner Intelligence owns

Unit-level capacity interpretation.
Partner risk.
Partner health.
Future advisor capacity interpretation.
Development-to-productivity bridge.
Capacity concentration risk.
Leadership gap.
Partner forecast inputs.
Unit sustainability interpretation.


### Productivity Intelligence owns

Advisor productivity metrics.
Activity-to-production interpretation.
Production efficiency.
Advisor output patterns.
Productivity thresholds.
Productivity trend.
Productive advisor classification.


### Partner Intelligence consumes from Productivity

Productive advisor count.
Advisor productivity trend.
Production distribution.
Activity-to-production conversion.
Productivity concentration.


### Productivity Intelligence consumes from Partner

Partner context.
Unit assignment.
Development context.
Recruitment cohort context.


### Boundary

### Productivity answers
Is this advisor or group producing effectively?

### Partner answers
Is this Partner building enough productive and durable capacity?

### Example

An advisor may be productive.
Productivity Intelligence explains that advisor's output.

A Partner may still be at risk if that productivity comes from one advisor and no future capacity exists.
Partner Intelligence explains that unit fragility.


## 12. Partner Vs Compensation

Partner Intelligence and Compensation Intelligence must remain separate.

### Compensation Intelligence explains

What was calculated.
What was earned.
What was paid.
What rules applied.
What period governed the payment.
Why the payout occurred.

### Partner Intelligence explains

Whether the Partner's commercial unit is healthy, durable and scalable.


Why a unit can appear successful in compensation but not be healthy:

Compensation is often lagging.
One advisor may create most of the payout.
A temporary production spike can inflate payout.
Rule Pack incentives may reward short-term behavior.
Recruitment may be collapsing.
Retention may be weak.
Development may be failing.
Future capacity may be empty.

### Therefore

High compensation is evidence.
It is not proof of unit health.


Why a unit can appear healthy and not yet reflect in compensation:

Recruitment pipeline may be strong but not yet signed.
Signed advisors may be developing but not yet producing.
Activity may be improving before production appears.
Retention may be improving before compensation reflects it.
Leadership capacity may be emerging before payout rules recognize it.

### Therefore

Low current compensation is not always failure.
It may be an early-stage capacity build.


### Boundary

Compensation owns payouts.
Partner owns unit health interpretation.

Partner Intelligence may consume compensation.
It must not calculate compensation.

Compensation may consume Partner assignments and Rule Pack context.
It must not define Partner health.


## 13. Partner Vs Business Planning

Partner Intelligence and Business Planning Intelligence are also separate.


### Partner Intelligence owns

Current and projected unit capacity interpretation.
Partner risk.
Partner health.
Unit sustainability.
Capacity bottlenecks.
Leadership gap.
Development load.


### Business Planning Intelligence owns

Goal to Forecast to Gap to Actions.
Plan feasibility.
Scenario planning.
Required activity plans.
Resource allocation.
Execution roadmap.


### Partner Intelligence consumes

Business goals.
Planning periods.
Target capacity.
Expected growth plan.


### Business Planning consumes

Partner health.
Recruitment capacity.
Development capacity.
Productive advisor capacity.
Partner risk.
Forecast gaps.
Concentration risk.


### Boundary

### Partner Intelligence answers
What is the condition of the Partner's unit?

### Business Planning answers
What must happen to reach a goal from the current condition?

### Example

### Partner Intelligence says
The unit has strong recruitment but weak development capacity.

### Business Planning says
To reach the goal, reduce signed-advisor overload, increase coaching cadence and prioritize first-productivity conversion.

Partner Intelligence provides diagnosis.
Business Planning converts diagnosis into plan.


## 14. Red Team Review

### Scenario 1
Many signed, 0 productivity.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence treats signed count as success, it fails.

### Correct interpretation
Recruitment conversion is strong, but development or productivity conversion is broken.

### Guardrail
Signed advisors must be separated from productive advisor capacity.


### Scenario 2
High production, 1 advisor.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence treats production total as unit health, it fails.

### Correct interpretation
Unit has productivity concentration risk and single advisor dependency.

### Guardrail
Measure distribution, not only total production.


### Scenario 3
Many advisors, low retention.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence treats headcount as capacity, it fails.

### Correct interpretation
Unit leaks capacity.
Recruitment may be replacing losses rather than compounding growth.

### Guardrail
Retention must be part of Partner health.


### Scenario 4
Much recruitment, no development.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence celebrates recruitment volume, it fails.

### Correct interpretation
Candidate supply is not becoming productive capacity.

### Guardrail
Recruitment output must be connected to signed, active and productive outcomes.


### Scenario 5
Much development, no recruitment.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence focuses only on current advisors, it misses future shortage.

### Correct interpretation
Current advisor base may improve, but future capacity pipeline is drying.

### Guardrail
Partner health must include future advisor capacity.


### Scenario 6
Star Partner, no successors.

### What breaks
If Partner Intelligence treats personal leadership as enough, it fails.

### Correct interpretation
Unit may depend on one leader and lack scalability.

### Guardrail
Leadership capacity and successor emergence must be visible.


### Scenario 7
High compensation, high fragility.

### What breaks
If compensation is treated as truth, Partner health is misread.

### Correct interpretation
Compensation is a lagging outcome and may hide concentration, retention or recruitment risk.

### Guardrail
Partner Intelligence must separate economic reward from structural health.


### Scenario 8
Low compensation, strong early pipeline.

### What breaks
If current payout is treated as failure, early capacity building is ignored.

### Correct interpretation
Partner may be building future value not yet reflected in compensation.

### Guardrail
Leading indicators must be preserved separately from lagging economics.


### Scenario 9
Many productive advisors, no recruitment.

### What breaks
If current productivity is treated as permanent, future decline is missed.

### Correct interpretation
The unit is currently strong but future capacity is at risk.

### Guardrail
Recruitment gap must remain visible even during strong production.


### Scenario 10
Many candidates from weak sources.

### What breaks
If candidate volume is treated as pipeline strength, the Partner appears healthier than reality.

### Correct interpretation
Source quality and conversion must govern pipeline interpretation.

### Guardrail
Recruitment source quality must feed Partner health.


### Red Team conclusion

Partner Intelligence holds only if it refuses to collapse the domain into:

Recruitment count.
Signed count.
Production total.
Compensation.
Promotion status.

Partner Intelligence must integrate capacity creation, capacity conversion, capacity distribution, capacity durability and capacity scalability.


## 15. Architecture Decision

### Partner Intelligence is

Domain.

### It is not merely

Subdomain.
Capability.
Interpretation.
Score.

### Justification

### Partner Intelligence has its own business question

Is the Partner building a sustainable commercial unit?

### It has its own inputs

Recruitment.
Development.
Productivity.
Retention.
Behavior.
Compensation.
Forecast.
Business plan context.

### It has its own outputs

Partner Health.
Partner Risk.
Productive Advisor Capacity.
Unit Growth.
Future Capacity Gap.
Development Capacity.
Leadership Capacity.
Partner Forecast inputs.

### It has its own ownership

Unit-level interpretation of capacity and sustainability.

### It does not own

Recruitment funnel.
Productivity metrics.
Compensation calculations.
Business plans.
Forecast orchestration.
Relationship Capital.
Market Natural.
P200.
Relationship Activation.

### Architecture status

ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE

### Reason

Partner Intelligence is clearly a domain, but it should not be locked yet.

### The discovery identifies the correct unit of analysis

Productive Advisor Capacity

However, Partner Intelligence depends on domains that are not yet locked:

Advisor Development Intelligence.
Productivity Intelligence.
Retention interpretation.
Leadership capacity.
Partner-specific Rule Pack rules.

Therefore, Partner Intelligence should advance from DISCOVERED to ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE, not ARCHITECTURE LOCK.


## 16. Recommended Next Step

## Recommended Next Step

Advisor Development Intelligence

### Justification

Recruitment is locked.
Partner Intelligence is now discovered as a domain and candidate.

### The biggest unresolved bridge is

Signed Advisor
to
Productive Advisor Capacity

That bridge is development.

Without Advisor Development Intelligence, Partner Intelligence cannot explain why:

Many signed advisors produce nothing.
Some advisors activate quickly.
Some advisors stall.
Some advisors become productive.
Some advisors leave.
Some advisors become future leaders.

Productivity Intelligence should come after Development because productivity is the output that development attempts to create.

Forecast Intelligence should come after Development and Productivity because forecasts need stable domain signals.

Business Planning should come after the key capacity domains are clearer because planning needs reliable diagnosis.

Compensation Intelligence already has foundation work, but Partner success cannot be reduced to compensation.

### Therefore

Next architecture PAQ should focus on Advisor Development Intelligence.

This does not create implementation approval.
It only identifies the next domain to clarify.


## 17. Final Verdict

Partner Intelligence exists.

It should be treated as a domain.

It is not Recruitment.
It is not Productivity.
It is not Compensation.
It is not Business Planning.
It is not Forecast Intelligence.

Partner Intelligence is the domain that explains whether a Partner is building sustainable commercial capacity through people.

### The phrase

"Un asesor es una franquicia.
La labor del Partner es abrir franquicias."

is approved as an operating model, not as literal architecture law.

### The stronger architectural formulation is

A Partner builds productive advisor capacity.

The advisor is not automatically a franchise.
The advisor becomes an economic unit only when development, activation, productivity and retention convert potential into durable output.

### Final status

ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE

### Reason

The domain boundary is clear enough to approve the domain candidate.
The core economic unit is clear enough to guide future architecture.
The domain still depends on Development and Productivity hardening before lock.

### Official Partner Intelligence question

Is this Partner creating enough productive, retained and scalable advisor capacity to sustain future commercial growth?

### Official unit of analysis

Productive Advisor Capacity

### Official leading signals

Relationship activation.
Recruitment pipeline.
Source quality.
Connected candidates.
Signed advisors.
Development activity.
Advisor activity.
Coaching behavior.
Source diversity.

### Official lagging signals

Productivity.
Production.
Retention.
Compensation.
Promotion.
Leadership emergence.

### Official non-owner boundaries

Recruitment owns candidate flow.
Productivity owns productivity metrics.
Compensation owns payouts.
Business Planning owns plans.
Forecast owns cross-domain forecast orchestration.
Mick owns behavior intelligence.
Relationship Capital, Market Natural, P200 and Relationship Activation remain upstream or transversal layers.

### Architecture conclusion

Partner Intelligence should move to ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE and wait for Advisor Development Intelligence and Productivity Intelligence before Architecture Lock.

Implementation remains not approved.
No code should be created from this document without a separate implementation authorization.



===== PAQ-08-ADVISOR-DEVELOPMENT-INTELLIGENCE-DISCOVERY.md =====

# PAQ-08 Advisor Development Intelligence Discovery

## Repository References

- [FORGE_MASTER_BUILD_TREE.md](FORGE_MASTER_BUILD_TREE.md)
- [AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md)
- [FORGE_CONSTITUTION_V3.md](FORGE_CONSTITUTION_V3.md)
- [FORGE_FOUNDATION_LOCK.md](FORGE_FOUNDATION_LOCK.md)

---


Forge OS
Principal Domain Architect Review
Advisor Development Intelligence Discovery

### Status
ARCHITECTURE CANDIDATE RECOMMENDED

### Scope
Architecture only.
No code.
No engines.
No schemas.
No UI.
No commits.


## 1. Executive Summary

Advisor Development Intelligence is the Forge domain responsible for explaining how a signed person becomes productive advisor capacity.

### It lives in the architectural gap

Candidate
Connected
Signed
Advisor Development
Productive Advisor Capacity

Recruitment creates candidate flow.
Precontract or Career confirms the person entered the advisor path.
Productivity measures economic output.

Advisor Development Intelligence explains the transformation between signing and productive output.

This domain exists because a signed advisor is not yet an economic unit.

### A signed advisor may

Never activate.
Activate but not learn.
Learn but not execute.
Execute but not convert.
Produce once and stop.
Produce but not retain behavior.
Become productive.
Become a future leader.

Without Advisor Development Intelligence, Forge would confuse signing with capacity.

That would break Partner Intelligence because Partner Intelligence identified the true unit as:

Productive Advisor Capacity

### Advisor Development Intelligence answers

Is this signed advisor becoming capable?
What is blocking transformation?
Is the advisor learning, executing and improving?
Is the Partner developing or only recruiting?
Which signed advisors are likely to produce?
Which advisors are at risk before lagging results appear?
Which behaviors and learning milestones predict productive capacity?

### Final discovery

Advisor Development Intelligence is not training.
It is not motivation.
It is not generic coaching.
It is not productivity.
It is not Mick.

Advisor Development Intelligence is the transformation domain that integrates learning, coaching, execution behavior, early commercial attempts and first results to determine whether a signed advisor is becoming productive commercial capacity.


## 2. Advisor Development Definition

### Development is

The measurable transformation of a signed advisor from potential commercial capacity into active, capable, consistent and eventually productive advisor capacity.

### Development is not merely

Training attendance.
Content completion.
Motivation.
Coaching sessions.
Activity volume.
First production.
Productivity.
Leadership.

### Development includes

Learning.
Behavior activation.
Skill acquisition.
Commercial execution.
Coachability.
Consistency.
First commercial attempts.
First production readiness.
Early adaptation.
Risk reduction.
Capacity formation.

Development is capacitación only in part.

Training provides knowledge.
Development proves whether knowledge becomes behavior and capability.

Development is entrenamiento only in part.

Training and practice matter, but development requires real-world execution.

Development is coaching only in part.

Coaching guides transformation, but the advisor must execute.

Development is activity only in part.

Activity is evidence of execution, but activity without learning or conversion may be noise.

Development is productivity only in part.

Productivity is an outcome of successful development, but the development domain starts before productivity appears.

Development is leadership only in part.

Leadership potential may emerge from development, but leadership is not required for every advisor to become productive.

Development is behavior only in part.

Behavior is measured by Mick.
Development interprets whether behavior is producing transformation.

### Operational definition

Advisor Development Intelligence owns the interpretation of whether a signed advisor is progressing from formal entry into the career toward productive advisor capacity through learning, coachability, activation, execution consistency and early commercial results.


## 3. Inputs

Advisor Development Intelligence consumes multiple inputs.

It does not own all of them.


Connected Candidates

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Recruitment and Precontract boundary.

### Dependency
Development needs connected context to understand candidate origin, source quality and precontract readiness before signing.

### Development interpretation
Was this person entering development with enough readiness and commitment?


Signed Advisors

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Career or Precontract lifecycle, depending on final domain ownership.

### Dependency
Development begins after formal signing or official advisor entry.

### Development interpretation
What happens after signing?
Does the signed person activate into advisor behavior?


Mick Signals

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Mick owns Behavior Intelligence.

### Dependency
Development needs behavior evidence: follow-up, activity, discipline, consistency, responsiveness and execution cadence.

### Development interpretation
Are behaviors becoming capability?


Activity Signals

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Mick may own behavior interpretation.
Productivity may consume activity-to-output signals.

### Dependency
Development needs early activity to detect activation and execution.

### Development interpretation
Is the advisor moving from passive learning to field execution?


Training Completion

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Training or Learning domain if formalized later.
In current architecture, Development consumes training evidence.

### Dependency
Development needs to know whether required learning actions occurred.

### Development interpretation
Did training completion translate into readiness or behavior?


Coaching Events

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Mick may own coaching behavior consistency.
Partner Intelligence consumes coaching capacity.
Development owns interpretation of advisor transformation after coaching.

### Dependency
Development needs coaching events to evaluate support, responsiveness and improvement.


Recruitment Context

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Recruitment Intelligence.

### Dependency
Development uses source, interview path, candidate quality and recruitment risk to understand initial expectations.

### Development interpretation
Did recruitment source or interview path predict development success?


Relationship Activation

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Transversal capability.

### Dependency
Advisor development requires relationship activation because early advisors must activate natural markets, referrals, CI and prospecting behavior.

### Development interpretation
Is the advisor converting relationship access into commercial activity?


Business Plans

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Business Planning Intelligence.

### Dependency
Development needs goals and expected activity plans to evaluate whether development pace supports the plan.

### Development interpretation
Is the advisor developing fast enough for the declared plan?


Partner Context

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Partner Intelligence and CommercialAssignment.

### Dependency
Development needs to know who is responsible for developing the advisor during each period.

### Development interpretation
Is the Partner developing the advisor effectively?


Rule Packs

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Rule Pack.

### Dependency
Development needs active rules for stages, requirements, milestones, eligibility, training windows and career periods.

### Development interpretation
Does the advisor meet development expectations under the active Rule Pack?


Career Stage

### Consume
Yes.

### Ownership
Career Intelligence.

### Dependency
Development expectations differ by career stage.

### Development interpretation
Is behavior and progress appropriate for this stage?


Inputs not owned by Development

Recruitment pipeline.
Compensation calculations.
Production event truth.
Productivity metric ownership.
Business plan ownership.
Behavior ownership.
Rule definitions.
Career official status.


## 4. Outputs

Advisor Development Intelligence produces transformation signals.


Development Progress

### Represents
How far the advisor has moved from signed status toward productive capacity.

### Inputs
Training, coaching, activity, relationship activation, early results, stage expectations.

### Nature
Interpretation.


Development Readiness

### Represents
Whether the advisor is ready for the next development demand.

### Examples
Ready for first appointments.
Ready for first production push.
Ready for consistency phase.
Ready for higher activity expectations.

### Nature
Interpretation.


First Production Readiness

### Represents
Whether the advisor has enough learning, activation and execution behavior to plausibly reach first production.

### Nature
Forecast-informed interpretation.

### Guardrail
Not a guarantee of production.


Advisor Activation Readiness

### Represents
Whether the advisor is ready to begin real market activation and commercial activity.

### Inputs
Training, confidence, relationship activation capacity, coaching, initial plan.


Coachability Signal

### Represents
Whether the advisor receives, applies and improves from coaching.

### Ownership
Shared boundary with Mick.

### Development owns
Transformation interpretation.

### Mick owns
Behavior evidence and consistency.


Behavior Consistency

### Represents
Observed consistency in execution.

### Ownership
Mick owns behavior metric.

### Development consumes
Whether consistency supports development progress.


Learning Progress

### Represents
Whether learning is occurring and becoming usable.

### Guardrail
Training completion is not equal to learning progress.


Productivity Readiness

### Represents
Whether the advisor appears ready to become productive.

### Inputs
Activity, first appointments, first production readiness, follow-up, prospecting, coaching response.

### Nature
Interpretation.


Retention Probability

### Represents
Estimated likelihood that advisor remains engaged through early development.

### Nature
Forecast.

### Guardrail
Must be presented as uncertainty, not fact.


Leadership Potential

### Represents
Early signal that an advisor may later become a leader or capacity multiplier.

### Nature
Weak interpretation at this stage.

### Guardrail
Development can surface early potential but should not own leadership qualification.


Development Risk

### Represents
Risk that the advisor will fail to become productive capacity.

### Examples
Activation failure.
Learning failure.
Coachability risk.
Inactivity risk.
Consistency risk.
Early attrition risk.
First production delay.


Development Bottleneck

### Represents
Where transformation is stuck.

### Examples
Training completed but no activity.
Activity happening but no appointments.
Appointments happening but no production.
First production achieved but not repeated.


## 5. Development Stages

Advisor development stages must represent transformation, not just administrative status.

### Conceptual model

Signed
Orientation
Activation
Learning
Field Execution
First Appointment
First Production
Repeat Activity
Consistency
Productive Advisor


Signed

### Meaning
Advisor has formally entered the career path.

### What it proves
Formal entry.

### What it does not prove
Skill, activity, productivity or retention.


Orientation

### Meaning
Advisor understands basic expectations, support structure, tools and initial path.

### What it proves
Initial exposure.

### What it does not prove
Execution.


Activation

### Meaning
Advisor begins doing the behaviors required to start commercial work.

### Examples
Activating Market Natural.
Preparing first contacts.
Starting prospecting.
Responding to coaching.

### What it proves
Movement from passive entry to action.


Learning

### Meaning
Advisor acquires and begins applying knowledge.

### Examples
Product basics.
Conversation basics.
Process basics.
Compliance or operational basics.

### What it proves
Knowledge formation only if tied to application.


Field Execution

### Meaning
Advisor begins real commercial activity with people.

### Examples
Contact attempts.
Appointments requested.
Follow-ups.
Referral asks.
Relationship activation.

### What it proves
Execution behavior.


First Appointment

### Meaning
Advisor creates a real commercial conversation.

### What it proves
Market activation is producing meetings.

### What it does not prove
Sales ability or productivity.


First Production

### Meaning
Advisor creates first production event.

### What it proves
The advisor crossed from learning/execution into economic output.

### What it does not prove
Consistency, durability or retained productivity.


Repeat Activity

### Meaning
Advisor continues executing after first result.

### What it proves
Potential for non-accidental progress.


Consistency

### Meaning
Advisor shows repeatable behaviors and early productive rhythm.

### What it proves
Development is becoming capacity.


Productive Advisor

### Meaning
Advisor demonstrates enough production and consistency under the active Rule Pack or domain definitions to count as productive capacity.

### Ownership
Productivity Intelligence owns final productivity classification.
Development owns readiness and transformation path into that state.


### Stage guardrails

These stages are conceptual.
Specific names, windows, requirements and thresholds belong to Rule Packs.


## 6. Coachability Review

### Hypothesis

Two people can receive exactly the same training.
One produces.
The other does not.

This is true.

### The difference may include

Coachability.
Discipline.
Execution.
Learning velocity.
Consistency.
Market quality.
Trust access.
Emotional resilience.
Follow-up behavior.
Partner support.


Coachability

### Meaning
The advisor's demonstrated ability to receive feedback, apply it, improve behavior and change outcomes.

### Coachability is not
Agreeing with the coach.
Attending coaching.
Being likeable.
Being motivated.

### Coachability is
Behavior change after feedback.
Improvement after correction.
Reduced repeated mistakes.
Faster adoption of useful practices.
Better execution after coaching.


Discipline

### Meaning
The advisor's ability to execute required behaviors consistently.

### Owner
Mick owns behavior discipline signals.

### Development consumes
Whether discipline produces transformation.


Execution

### Meaning
The advisor actually performs commercial actions.

### Owner
Mick owns behavior evidence.

### Development consumes
Whether execution advances development stage.


Learning Velocity

### Meaning
How quickly the advisor turns instruction into usable field behavior.

### Owner
Advisor Development.

### Inputs
Training, coaching, behavior change, outcomes.


Consistency

### Meaning
Repeatable execution over time.

### Owner
Mick owns consistency behavior.
Development interprets whether consistency supports capacity formation.


### Ownership decision

Coachability belongs to both Mick and Development, but at different layers.

### Mick owns
Behavior evidence.
Response to coaching as observable behavior.
Consistency.
Execution pattern.

### Advisor Development owns
Coachability as transformation signal.
Learning velocity.
Development improvement.
Whether coaching creates capability.

### Partner Intelligence consumes
Coachability across advisors to evaluate development capacity.


## 7. Development Vs Mick

Mick and Advisor Development must be separated.

Mick measures behavior.
Advisor Development measures transformation.


### Mick owns

Activity behavior.
Consistency.
Follow-up discipline.
Coaching responsiveness as behavior.
Prospecting rhythm.
Relationship activation behavior.
Task completion.
Execution pattern.
Behavior risk.


### Advisor Development owns

Development progress.
Development readiness.
Learning progress.
Coachability as transformation.
First production readiness.
Productivity readiness.
Development risk.
Development bottleneck.
Signed-to-productive transformation.


### Mick consumes

Development expectations.
Development stage context.
Required behaviors for current stage.


### Advisor Development consumes

Mick behavior signals.
Activity consistency.
Execution evidence.
Behavior risk.


### Boundary example

Advisor made 20 calls.

### Mick says
The advisor executed the activity.

### Advisor Development says
The activity did or did not advance the advisor from activation to field execution or appointment creation.


### Boundary example

Advisor attended coaching and changed behavior.

### Mick says
Advisor responded to coaching and executed changed behavior.

### Advisor Development says
Coachability improved development trajectory.


### Anti-pattern

Do not let Development become a behavior tracker.
Do not let Mick become a development domain.


## 8. Development Vs Productivity

Advisor Development and Productivity Intelligence are sequential and overlapping, but not the same.


### Advisor Development owns

Transformation into capability.
Readiness for productivity.
Early learning and execution path.
First production readiness.
Development risk.
Coachability interpretation.
Development bottlenecks.


### Productivity Intelligence owns

Production effectiveness.
Activity-to-output performance.
Advisor productivity metrics.
Productive advisor classification.
Production consistency.
Output quality and efficiency.
Productivity trends.


### Where development ends

Development ends when the advisor has enough consistent capability and output evidence to be evaluated primarily as a productive advisor.

The exact threshold belongs to Rule Pack or Productivity domain definitions.


### Where productivity begins

Productivity begins when real commercial output can be evaluated as recurring performance rather than isolated development milestone.


### Shared signals

Activity.
Appointments.
First production.
Repeat production.
Consistency.
Pipeline.
Follow-up.
Market activation.


### Signals Development interprets

Is this advisor learning?
Is the advisor moving to the next stage?
Is first production likely?
Is the advisor coachable?
What is blocking transformation?


### Signals Productivity interprets

Is the advisor producing effectively?
Is output efficient?
Is production repeatable?
Is activity converting?
Is the advisor productive under the active rules?


### Boundary example

First production occurs.

### Development says
Advisor crossed a critical milestone.

### Productivity says
Not enough evidence yet to classify durable productivity.


### Boundary example

Advisor produces consistently for multiple periods.

### Development says
Development succeeded or matured.

### Productivity says
Advisor is productive and should be evaluated on output performance.


## 9. First Production Analysis

First production is important because it is the first hard evidence that a signed advisor can turn learning and activity into economic output.

### It is

An event when the production event occurs.
A milestone in the development journey.
Evidence of transformation.
A signal of capability.
A predictor candidate, not a guarantee.

### It is not

Proof of consistency.
Proof of retention.
Proof of full productivity.
Proof of future compensation.
Proof of leadership potential.


### What first production really means

The advisor has crossed the psychological and operational boundary from preparation to economic creation.

### It may validate

Market activation.
Product understanding.
Conversation skill.
Follow-up.
Coachability.
Execution.
Partner support.

### It may also be accidental

One warm lead.
One easy case.
One Partner-assisted sale.
One inherited opportunity.

### Therefore

First production must be interpreted with context.

### Important contextual questions

Where did the first production come from?
Was it advisor-generated?
Was it Partner-assisted?
Was it from Market Natural?
Was it from a referral?
Was it repeatable?
How long did it take?
What activity preceded it?
What coaching preceded it?
What happened after?


### What first production predicts

Potential for productive capacity.
Validation of early development path.
Possible increase in confidence.
Reduced early attrition risk.
Better forecast confidence if paired with behavior consistency.


### What first production does not predict alone

Long-term productivity.
Retention.
Consistency.
Leadership.
Compensation.
Qualification.


## Architecture Decision

FIRST_PRODUCTION should be treated as both:

### Fact event
Production occurred.

### Development milestone
Advisor crossed first economic output boundary.

Development does not own the production fact.
Production Events own the fact.
Development owns the milestone interpretation.


## 10. Development Failure Model

Development failure is when a signed advisor does not become productive advisor capacity.


### Failure pattern
Signed, never activates.

### Root causes
Weak commitment.
Poor expectation setting.
Fear of market activation.
Low Partner follow-up.
No clear first actions.

### Symptoms
No activity.
No coaching engagement.
No relationship activation.
No appointments.

### Consequences
Signed advisor remains non-economic.
Partner capacity is overstated.


### Failure pattern
Activates, never schedules.

### Root causes
Poor contact skill.
